</head> <body class="mediawiki ltr sitedir-ltr ns-0 ns-subject page-PlayStation_3_models skin-vector action-view vector-animateLayout">   <div id="mw-page-base" class="noprint"></div>   <div id="mw-head-base" class="noprint"></div>   <div id="content" class="mw-body" role="main">    <a id="top"></a>         <div id="siteNotice"><!-- CentralNotice --></div>       <h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en"><span dir="auto">PlayStation 3 models</span></h1>       <div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">          <div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>         <div id="contentSub"></div>             <div id="jump-to-nav" class="mw-jump">      Jump to:     <a href="#mw-navigation">navigation</a>,      <a href="#p-search">search</a>     </div>     <div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><p>The <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_3" title="PlayStation 3">PlayStation 3</a> video game console has been produced in various models during its life cycle. At launch, the PlayStation 3 was available with either a 20, 40, 60, or 80&#160;GB hard disk drive in the US and Japan, priced from US$499 to US$599; and with either a 40, 60, or 80&#160;GB hard disk drive in Europe, priced from £299 to £425.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> Since then, Sony have released two further redesigned models, the "Slim" and "Super Slim" models. Total number of sold consoles(up to end of December 2013) is estimated at 77 million.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup></p> <p></p> <div id="toc" class="toc"> <div id="toctitle"> <h2>Contents</h2> </div> <ul> <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Original_model"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">Original model</span></a></li> <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2"><a href="#Slim_model"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Slim model</span></a></li> <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-3"><a href="#Super_Slim_model"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Super Slim model</span></a></li> <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-4"><a href="#Model_comparison"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Model comparison</span></a></li> <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-5"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li> </ul> </div> <p></p> <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Original_model">Original model</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=PlayStation_3_models&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Original model">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> <div class="thumb tright"> <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:PS3-Fat-Console-Vert.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/PS3-Fat-Console-Vert.jpg/170px-PS3-Fat-Console-Vert.jpg" width="170" height="290" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/PS3-Fat-Console-Vert.jpg/255px-PS3-Fat-Console-Vert.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/PS3-Fat-Console-Vert.jpg/340px-PS3-Fat-Console-Vert.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2160" data-file-height="3680" /></a> <div class="thumbcaption"> <div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:PS3-Fat-Console-Vert.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div> 60&#160;GB model</div> </div> </div> <p>There are several original PlayStation 3 hardware models, which are commonly referred to by the size of their included <a href="/wiki/Hard_disk_drive" title="Hard disk drive">hard disk drive</a>: 20, 40, 60, 80 or 160&#160;GB.<sup id="cite_ref-IGNPS3E32006_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IGNPS3E32006-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SCEAPS3comparison_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SCEAPS3comparison-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> Although referred to by their HDD size, the capabilities of the consoles vary by region and release date. The only difference in the appearance of the first five models was the color of the trim, number of USB ports, the presence or absence of a door (which covers the flash card readers on equipped models) and some minor changes to the air vents. All retail packages include one or two <a href="/wiki/Sixaxis" title="Sixaxis">Sixaxis</a> controllers and/or a <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_3_accessories#DualShock_3" title="PlayStation 3 accessories">DualShock 3</a> controller (beginning June 12, 2008<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup>), one miniUSB to USB cable (for connecting the controller and <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_Portable" title="PlayStation Portable">PlayStation Portable</a> to the system), one <a href="/wiki/Composite_video" title="Composite video">composite video</a>/stereo audio output cable, one Ethernet cable (20, 60 and CECHExx 80&#160;GB only) and one <a href="/wiki/Power_cable" title="Power cable">power cable</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SCEAPS3comparison_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SCEAPS3comparison-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> All models support software emulation of the original PlayStation,<sup id="cite_ref-40GB_GameSpot_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40GB_GameSpot-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ps1_softwareBC_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ps1_softwareBC-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> but support for PlayStation 2 backward compatibility diminished with later compatible models and the last model to have integrated backward compatibility was the NTSC 80&#160;GB (CECHE) Metal Gear Solid 4 Bundle.<sup id="cite_ref-PS3FAQs_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PS3FAQs-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> Compatibility issues with games for both systems are detailed in a public database hosted by the manufacturer.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> All models, excluding the 20&#160;GB model, include <a href="/wiki/IEEE_802.11" title="IEEE 802.11">802.11 b/g</a> <a href="/wiki/Wi-Fi" title="Wi-Fi">Wi-Fi</a>.</p> <p>In addition to all of the features of the 20&#160;GB model, the 60&#160;GB model has internal IEEE 802.11 b/g Wi-Fi, multiple flash card readers (SD/MultiMedia Card, CompactFlash Type I/Type II, Microdrive,<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> Memory Stick/PRO/Duo) and a chrome colored trim.<sup id="cite_ref-specs_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-specs-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> In terms of hardware, the 80&#160;GB model CECHE released in <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a> is identical to the 60&#160;GB model CECHC released in the PAL regions, except for the difference in hard drive size.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> The European 60GB model (CECHC), the South Korean and North American CECHE 80GB model excludes the <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_2" title="PlayStation 2">PlayStation 2</a> "<a href="/wiki/Emotion_Engine" title="Emotion Engine">Emotion Engine</a>" CPU chip with it being replaced by an emulated version via the Cell Broadband Engine.<sup id="cite_ref-PS3FAQs_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PS3FAQs-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> However, it retains the "Graphics Synthesizer" GPU resulting in a hybrid hardware and software emulation.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> Due to <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_3_games#Removal_of_hardware_support" title="PlayStation 3 games" class="mw-redirect">the elimination</a> of the "Emotion Engine" and its replacement with a software-emulated version, the level of PlayStation 2 compatibility was slightly reduced.<sup id="cite_ref-PS3FAQs_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PS3FAQs-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> The 40&#160;GB, 80&#160;GB (CECHL,CECHM,and CECHK) and 160&#160;GB models have two USB ports instead of the four USB ports on other models and do not include multiple flash card readers, <a href="/wiki/Super_Audio_CD" title="Super Audio CD">SACD</a> support,<sup id="cite_ref-ps3sacd_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ps3sacd-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> or backward compatibility with PlayStation 2 games.<sup id="cite_ref-PS3FAQs_11-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PS3FAQs-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CNETReview_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNETReview-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> This was due to the removal of "Graphics Synthesizer" GPU, which stripped the units of all PlayStation 2 based hardware.<sup id="cite_ref-SCEE_40GB_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SCEE_40GB-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-E30880GB_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-E30880GB-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p> <p>No official Wi-Fi or flash <a href="/wiki/Memory_card" title="Memory card">memory card</a> readers were ever released by Sony for the 20&#160;GB system, although Sony had plans to do so.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> As of September 2009, Sony had placed no further emphasis on these proposed add-ons.<sup id="cite_ref-E30880GB_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-E30880GB-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> Nevertheless, as the model features four USB 2.0 ports, <a href="/wiki/Wireless_network" title="Wireless network">wireless networking</a> and flash memory card support can already be obtained through the use of widely available external USB adapters and third-party PS3-specific media hubs.<sup id="cite_ref-PS3FAQs_11-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PS3FAQs-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></p> <p>It was rumored that the Cell processors in the third-generation PS3s (40&#160;GB, 2008 80&#160;GB (CECHL,CECHM,CECHK) and 160&#160;GB) would move from a 90&#160;nm process to the newer 65&#160;nm process,<sup id="cite_ref-Cell65LowerPower_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cell65LowerPower-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> which SCEI CEO Kaz Hirai later confirmed,<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> and later to 45&#160;nm. This change lowers the <a href="/wiki/Energy_conservation" title="Energy conservation">power consumption</a> of the console and makes it less expensive to produce.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup><br style="clear:both;" /></p> <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Slim_model">Slim model</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=PlayStation_3_models&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Slim model">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> <div class="thumb tright"> <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:PS3-Slim-Console-Vert.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/PS3-Slim-Console-Vert.jpg/170px-PS3-Slim-Console-Vert.jpg" width="170" height="257" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/PS3-Slim-Console-Vert.jpg/255px-PS3-Slim-Console-Vert.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/PS3-Slim-Console-Vert.jpg/340px-PS3-Slim-Console-Vert.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2220" data-file-height="3360" /></a> <div class="thumbcaption"> <div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:PS3-Slim-Console-Vert.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div> 120&#160;GB Slim model</div> </div> </div> <p>The redesigned, slimmer version of the PlayStation 3 (commonly referred to as the "PS3 Slim" and officially branded "PS3") features an upgradeable 120&#160;GB, 160&#160;GB,<sup id="cite_ref-Torne2500_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Torne2500-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-JPWhiteSlim_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JPWhiteSlim-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> 250&#160;GB or 320&#160;GB<sup id="cite_ref-Torne2500_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Torne2500-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-JPWhiteSlim_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JPWhiteSlim-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> hard drive and is 32% smaller, 36% lighter and consumes 34% (CECH-20xx) or 45% (CECH-21xx) less power than the previous model,<sup id="cite_ref-PS3SlimPressRelease_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PS3SlimPressRelease-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PS3SlimSpecs_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PS3SlimSpecs-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> or one third of the original PS3 model. The Cell microprocessor has moved to a <a href="/wiki/45_nm" title="45 nm" class="mw-redirect">45&#160;nm</a> manufacturing process, which lets it run cooler and quieter than previous models, and the cooling system has been redesigned.<sup id="cite_ref-ArsTechnicaInterview_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ArsTechnicaInterview-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/RSX_%27Reality_Synthesizer%27" title="RSX 'Reality Synthesizer'">RSX</a> moved to a 40&#160;nm process<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> in the latest revision. The PS3 slim also includes support for <a href="/wiki/High-Definition_Multimedia_Interface#CEC" title="High-Definition Multimedia Interface" class="mw-redirect">CEC</a> (more commonly referred to by its manufacturer brandings of BraviaSync, VIERA Link, EasyLink etc.) which allows control of the console over HDMI by using the TV's remote control. The PS3 Slim no longer has the "main power" switch like the previous PS3 models, similar to redesigned <a href="/wiki/Slim_PlayStation_2" title="Slim PlayStation 2" class="mw-redirect">slimline PlayStation 2</a>. Support for emulation to play PS2 titles is not present in the Slim version, however shortly after the release of the PS3 slim, Sony announced a new series of PS2 remasters called <a href="/wiki/Classics_HD" title="Classics HD" class="mw-redirect">Classics HD</a> as in PS2 and PSP titles remastered in HD for the PS3 with trophies added and sometimes <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_Move" title="PlayStation Move">PlayStation Move</a> compatibility.<sup id="cite_ref-PS3SlimPressRelease_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PS3SlimPressRelease-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PS3SlimSpecs_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PS3SlimSpecs-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> As of October 2011, PS2 classics are available for purchase in the PlayStation Store.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></p> <p>The PS3 slim was officially released on September 1, 2009, in North America and Europe and on September 3, 2009, in Japan, Australia and New Zealand.<sup id="cite_ref-PS3SlimPressRelease_27-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PS3SlimPressRelease-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PS3SlimSpecs_28-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PS3SlimSpecs-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PS3SlimPressReleaseAU_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PS3SlimPressReleaseAU-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> However, some retailers such as <a href="/wiki/Amazon.com" title="Amazon.com">Amazon.com</a>, <a href="/wiki/Best_Buy" title="Best Buy">Best Buy</a> and <a href="/wiki/GameStop" title="GameStop">GameStop</a> started to sell the PS3 slim on August 25, 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> The PS3 Slim sold in excess of a million units in its first 3 weeks on sale.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> A 250&#160;GB <i>Final Fantasy XIII</i>-themed PS3 Slim, which was white in color with pink designs, was officially announced on September 24, 2009 at the <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Game_Show" title="Tokyo Game Show">Tokyo Game Show</a> as part of a bundle in Japan for <i><a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_XIII" title="Final Fantasy XIII">Final Fantasy XIII</a></i>, it was initially revealed in U.S. <a href="/wiki/Federal_Communications_Commission" title="Federal Communications Commission">Federal Communications Commission</a> (FCC) filings as the PS3 CECH-2000B.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> Sony Computer Entertainment Australia also announced later that day that it would be bringing the 250&#160;GB PS3 slim to Australia which would be bundled with other games and will not feature the <i>Final Fantasy XIII</i> theme. Although no North American bundles have been announced for the 250&#160;GB PS3 slim, it is sold as a stand-alone console in North America.<sup id="cite_ref-Slim_250GB_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Slim_250GB-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup></p> <p>In July 2010, Sony announced two new sizes of Slim PS3, 160&#160;GB and 320&#160;GB, with the 120&#160;GB model being discontinued in Japan.<sup id="cite_ref-JPWhiteSlim_26-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JPWhiteSlim-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> These were launched on July 29, 2010, in Japan, with the 160&#160;GB version available in "Classic White" as well as the standard "Charcoal Black".<sup id="cite_ref-JPWhiteSlim_26-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JPWhiteSlim-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> The black 160&#160;GB version was also made available as a bundle with the Japan-only DVR accessory <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_3_accessories#torne" title="PlayStation 3 accessories">torne</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Torne2500_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Torne2500-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> It was later announced that the new sizes were to be launched in other regions, with the 160&#160;GB model available from August 2010 in North America<sup id="cite_ref-160-320GB-US_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160-320GB-US-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> and October 2010 in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-160-320GB-EU_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160-320GB-EU-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> The 320&#160;GB model is to be available in North America only as part of a bundle with <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_Move" title="PlayStation Move">PlayStation Move</a>, a <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_Eye" title="PlayStation Eye">PlayStation Eye</a> and a copy of <a href="/wiki/Sports_Champions" title="Sports Champions">Sports Champions</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-160-320GB-US_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160-320GB-US-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> and in Europe with <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_Move" title="PlayStation Move">PlayStation Move</a>, a <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_Eye" title="PlayStation Eye">PlayStation Eye</a> and a demo disc.<sup id="cite_ref-160-320GB-EU_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160-320GB-EU-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> The bundles were released on September 19, 2010, and September 15, 2010, respectively, to coincide with the launch of PlayStation Move.<sup id="cite_ref-160-320GB-US_41-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160-320GB-US-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-160-320GB-EU_42-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160-320GB-EU-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup></p> <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Super_Slim_model">Super Slim model</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=PlayStation_3_models&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Super Slim model">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> <div class="thumb tright"> <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Garnet_Red_PS3_Super_Slim.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Garnet_Red_PS3_Super_Slim.jpg/150px-Garnet_Red_PS3_Super_Slim.jpg" width="150" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Garnet_Red_PS3_Super_Slim.jpg/225px-Garnet_Red_PS3_Super_Slim.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Garnet_Red_PS3_Super_Slim.jpg/300px-Garnet_Red_PS3_Super_Slim.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="2560" /></a> <div class="thumbcaption"> <div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Garnet_Red_PS3_Super_Slim.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div> 500&#160;GB garnet red PS3 Super Slim</div> </div> </div> <p>In September 2012, Sony announced that a new slimmer PS3 redesign (CECH-4000) was due to be released in late 2012 and that it would be available with either a 250&#160;GB or 500&#160;GB hard drive.<sup id="cite_ref-PCWorldSuperSlim_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PCWorldSuperSlim-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup></p> <p>In PAL regions, the 250&#160;GB model is not available; a model with 12&#160;GB of flash memory (CECH-4000A) is available in its place.<sup id="cite_ref-EurogamerSuperSlim_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EurogamerSuperSlim-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> A standalone 250&#160;GB hard drive (CECH-ZHD1) is available to upgrade this model.<sup id="cite_ref-EurogamerSuperSlim_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EurogamerSuperSlim-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SonySuperSlim_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SonySuperSlim-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> In the UK, the 500&#160;GB model was released on September 28, 2012,<sup id="cite_ref-EurogamerSuperSlim_44-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EurogamerSuperSlim-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> while the 12&#160;GB model was made available on October 12, 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-EurogamerSuperSlim_44-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EurogamerSuperSlim-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup></p> <p>CECH-4000B consoles (those with hard drives) weigh approximately 2.1&#160;kg (4.6&#160;lb),<sup id="cite_ref-PCWorldSuperSlim_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PCWorldSuperSlim-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EurogamerSuperSlim_44-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EurogamerSuperSlim-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> while the CECH-4000A weighs approximately 2.0&#160;kg (4.4&#160;lb).<sup id="cite_ref-SonySuperSlim_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SonySuperSlim-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> Both are roughly 25% smaller and about 20% lighter than the original PS3 Slim. This version has a sliding disc cover rather than the slot-loading drive found on previous PlayStation 3 consoles.</p> <p>A vertical stand (CECH-ZST1J) is also available for these models and launched on the same day as the consoles in their respective regions.<sup id="cite_ref-SonySuperSlim_45-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SonySuperSlim-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup></p> glossy finish<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208"><span>[</span>208<span>]</span></a></sup></b><br /> <b>All models include: <a href="/wiki/Blu-ray_Disc" title="Blu-ray Disc">Blu-ray</a>/<a href="/wiki/DVD" title="DVD">DVD</a>/<a href="/wiki/CD" title="CD" class="mw-redirect">CD</a> drive, <a href="/wiki/High-Definition_Multimedia_Interface" title="High-Definition Multimedia Interface" class="mw-redirect">HDMI 1.3a</a><sup id="cite_ref-pr_20.C2.A0GB_HDMI_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pr_20.C2.A0GB_HDMI-209"><span>[</span>209<span>]</span></a></sup> (upgraded to HDMI 1.4 via firmware update), <a href="/wiki/Bluetooth_2.0" title="Bluetooth 2.0" class="mw-redirect">Bluetooth 2.0</a>, Gigabit Ethernet (<a href="/wiki/10BASE-T" title="10BASE-T" class="mw-redirect">10BASE-T</a>, <a href="/wiki/100BASE-TX" title="100BASE-TX" class="mw-redirect">100BASE-TX</a>, <a href="/wiki/1000BASE-T" title="1000BASE-T" class="mw-redirect">1000BASE-T</a>) and <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_(console)" title="PlayStation (console)">PlayStation</a> backward compatibility through software emulation.</b><sup id="cite_ref-40GB_GameSpot_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40GB_GameSpot-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ps1_softwareBC_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ps1_softwareBC-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup><br /> <b>Model numbers differ by region. See <i><a href="/wiki/PlayStation_3_hardware#Model_numbers" title="PlayStation 3 hardware" class="mw-redirect">PlayStation 3 hardware – model numbers</a></i> for details.</b></p> <p><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_a"><b><a href="#ref_a">^</a></b></span> <b>a</b> Linux support removed in firmware version 3.21. See <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_3#OtherOS_support" title="PlayStation 3">OtherOS support</a> for details<br /> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_b"><b><a href="#ref_b">^</a></b></span> <b>b</b> Ceramic white model available in Asia and Japan only.<br /> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_c"><b><a href="#ref_c">^</a></b></span> <b>c</b> Satin silver model available in Asia and Japan only.<br /> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_d"><b><a href="#ref_d">^</a></b></span> <b>d</b> Gun-Metal Gray model is only available as part of the <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_Solid_4:_Guns_of_the_Patriots" title="Metal Gear Solid 4: Guns of the Patriots">MGS4</a></i> bundle.<br /> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_e"><b><a href="#ref_e">^</a></b></span> <b>e</b> <i><a href="/wiki/Yakuza_3" title="Yakuza 3">Yakuza 3</a></i> bundle features a Ceramic White model with custom grey dragon designs on its case. This version had a limited run of 10,000 units.<sup id="cite_ref-Yakuza3limited_92-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yakuza3limited-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210"><span>[</span>210<span>]</span></a></sup><br /> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_f"><b><a href="#ref_f">^</a></b></span> <b>f</b> "Cloud Black" (dark grey) console is only available as part of a Japanese limited edition <i><a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_VII:_Advent_Children" title="Final Fantasy VII: Advent Children">Final Fantasy VII: Advent Children</a></i> bundle and features a custom white design on the console<sup id="cite_ref-FFVIIBundle_106-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FFVIIBundle-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup><br /> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_g"><b><a href="#ref_g">^</a></b></span> <b>g</b> White and Pink model is only available as part of the Japanese <i><a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_XIII" title="Final Fantasy XIII">Final Fantasy XIII</a></i> bundle and features a pink design of Final Fantasy XIII character "<a href="/wiki/Lightning_(Final_Fantasy)" title="Lightning (Final Fantasy)">Lightning</a>" on its case.<br /> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_h"><b><a href="#ref_h">^</a></b></span> <b>h</b> Titanium Blue model is only available as part of the Japanese <i><a href="/wiki/Gran_Turismo_5" title="Gran Turismo 5">Gran Turismo 5</a> Titanium Blue</i> bundle&lt;<sup id="cite_ref-BlueGT5Bundle_136-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BlueGT5Bundle-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup><br /> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_i"><b><a href="#ref_i">^</a></b></span> <b>i</b> Magical Gold model is only available as part of the Japanese <a href="/wiki/Ni_no_Kuni" title="Ni no Kuni">Ni no Kuni</a> bundle<sup id="cite_ref-NinokuniBundle_149-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NinokuniBundle-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup><br /> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_j"><b><a href="#ref_j">^</a></b></span> <b>j</b> Black and Pink model is only available as part of the Japanese <i><a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_XIII-2" title="Final Fantasy XIII-2">Final Fantasy XIII-2</a></i> bundle and features a pink design of Final Fantasy XIII character "<a href="/wiki/Lightning_(Final_Fantasy)" title="Lightning (Final Fantasy)">Lightning</a>" on its case.<sup id="cite_ref-Final_Fantasy_XIII-2_bundle_159-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Final_Fantasy_XIII-2_bundle-159"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup><br /> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_l"><b><a href="#ref_l">^</a></b></span> <b>l</b> Black and Gold model is only available as part of the Japanese <i><a href="/wiki/Ry%C5%AB_ga_Gotoku_5" title="Ryū ga Gotoku 5">Yakuza 5</a></i> bundle and features a gold emblem design on its case.<sup id="cite_ref-Yakuza_5_bundle_193-1" class="reference"><a
